71\. indeque conspexit ambos, Madhuem–*et* Kaitabhum, pravis–ani–mis, peringenti–robore *praeditos*, irâ–rubris–oculis, devorare Brah–

72\. mum innisos. Exsurgens deinde cum ambobus dimicabat almus

73\. Haris, quinque–millia–annorum bracchia–vibrans excelsus. Ambo etiam ingenti–robore–dementes, Mahâmâyâ–perturbati allocuti sunt: ,,gratia nobis concedatur,'' sic Pulcricomem.

**Almum numen dixit:**

74\. ,,Estote iam mecum contenti, a me occidendi ambo etiam, quorsum ,,alia gratia heic, hoc enim electum *est* a me.''

**Sapiens dixit:**

75\. Ab ambobus optantibus ita tunc, universo ex aquis–constante mundo

76\. conspecto, appellatus *est* almus loto–similibus–oculis. Laeti *sumus* nos de tua pugna, honorifica abs te mors nobis, nos neca non quo

77\. terra aquâ *est* circumfusa. ,,Sic *esto*''; ita cum dixisset almus concham–discum–clavam–gerens, posita in ventre capita amborum disco

78\. fissa sunt. Ita illa exorta *est* a Brahmo celebrata ipso, potentiam huius Deae autem ulterius audi, enarrabo tibi.

**—————**

**CANTUS II.**

**———**

**Sapiens dixit:**

1\. Deorum–*et* Asurorum erat bellum per continuum saeculum olim,

2\. Mahischo Asurorum duce, Deorumque Indro. Tum ab Asuris pervalidis Deorum–exercitus victus *est*; victisque omnibus diis Indrus

3\. factus erat Mahischus–Asurus. Deinde devicti dii, loto–exortum Pradschâpatem ducem–constituentes, profecti *sunt* eo quo *erant* Isus et

4\. Garudadhvadschus (Vischnu). Sicut acciderat, ambobus ita a Mahischâsuro–commotam tredecim narrarunt Deorum–caedem–universam.

5\. ,,Sûryi–Indri–Agnis–Anili–Induis, Yami, Varunique, reliquorumque

6\. ,,potestates ille ipse profecto transgreditur. E coelo expulsi omnes ,,ab isto Deorum–catervae in terra circumvagantur sicut mortales,

7\. ,,a Mahischo pravo. Hic vobis narratus est totus immortalium– ,,hostis–nisus, supplices nos aggressi *sumus*, interitus illius perpen–

8\. ,,datur.'' Sic auditis Deorum sermonibus, Madhuis–interfector, iratus est atque Sambhus, superciliorum–contractione–torvum–vul–

9\. tum *habentes*. Deinde summa–ira–impleti, disciferi ore tunc

10\. prodiit magnus splendor Brahmi Sangkarique; e reliquorum quoque deorum Sakro–duce corporibus profectus est permagnus splen–

11\. dor idemque in unitatem congressus est. Ingentis–splendoris cacumen fulgentem uti montem viderunt illi Suri ibi fulgore–penetrans–

12\. plagas–*et* spatium. Incomparabilis ibi *erat* ille splendor omnium–deorum–corporibus–exortus, in uno–consistens ille factus est fe–

13\. mina, penetrans–trimundum fulgore. Qui erat Sâmbhi splendor, ex hoc procreatus est illius–vultus, e Yamoque erant capelli, bra–

14\. chia e Vischnuis–splendore, e Somo *erat* mammarum par, me–diumque corpus ex Indro erat, e Varunoque *erant* crura–et femo–

15\. ra, clunes e splendore Terrae, e Brahmi–splendore *erant* pe–des, eorum–digiti e solis–splendore, e Vasuumque *splendore* digiti,

16\. e Kuveroque nasus. Illius autem dentes orti *erant* ex animan–tium–domini splendore, oculorum–trinitas exorta est etiam Pâvaci–

17\. splendore. Supercilia diluculi et crepusculi *erant* splendor, aures, Anili, reliquorumque Deorum coniunctio splendorum *erat* Siva.

18\. Deinde omnium–Deorum splendoris–cumulo–exortam illam conspi–

19\. cientes gaudium nacti sunt immortales a Mahischo–vexati. Tunc Dii dederunt illi sua quaeque tela, clavam clavâ protrahens dedit

20\. illi Arcifer (Sivus); discumque dedit Krischnus eiiciens e suo–

21\. disco, conchamque Varunus, hastam dedit illi Hutâsanus. Mâru–tus dedit arcum sagittis–impletas quoque pharetras–duas, fulmen

22\. Indrus eiiciens e *suo* fulmine immortalium–princeps. Dedit illi mille–oculis–*praeditus* tintinnabulum Airâvati elephanti; e temporis–

23\. sceptro Yamus sceptrum, funemque aquarum–dominus dedit. Ani–mantium–dominus rosarium dedit, Brahmus ollam fictilem, in om–

24\. nibus–pilorum–foveis proprios–radios luminis *dedit* Sol. Kâlusque (Yamus) dedit ensem illi, scutumque purum, Kschîrodusque (lactis–oceanus) immaculatum sertum et duas haud–detritas quoque vestes.

25\. Diadema etiam coeleste, duos–annulos *de auricula suspensos*, atque armillas, semi–lunam quoque splendidam et armillas in omnibus–

26\. brachiis. *Pedum* ornamenta nitida itidem, monile praestantissi–

27\. mum, annulos–gemmosos in omnibus digitis etiam. Visvakarman de–dit illi securim etiam valde–splendidam, tela multiformia atque haud–

28\. findendum thoracem; non–flaccidis–lotis *praeditam* coronam in capite, et pectore aliam dedit oceanus illi, atque lotum persplendi–

29\. dam. Himavan vectorem *dedit* leonem gemmas variasque, dedit

30\. repletum nectare poculum divitiarum–dominus (Kuverus); Seschus–que omnium–serpentum–dominus, magnis–gemmis–ornatam e serpentibus–*confectam* coronam dedit illi *is*, qui sustinet hanc terram.

31\. A reliquis quoque Diis Devia ornamentis et armis honorata, edidit

32\. alte illa risum iterum iterumque. Huius strepitu terribili universus repletus *erat* aër, immenso *et* permagno *strepitu* clamor–repercussus

33\. ingens erat. Agitati sunt omnes mundi mariaque contremuerunt,

34\. movebat se terra, vacillabant omnesque montes. ,,Victoria'', sic Dii gaudio hanc allocuti sunt leone–vectam; laudabant sapientesque

35\. illam veneratione–incurvatis–corporibus. Conspicientes universum agitatum trimundum immortalium–hostes, instructae omnes copiae

36\. exsurgebant sublatis–telis. ,,Eheu! quid istud,'' sic iratus vociferando Mahischus–Asurus accurrebat ad illum strepitum, ab omnibus

37\. Asuris circumdatus. Hic vidit deinde Deviam penetrantem–trimundum splendore, pedum–incessu–incurvantem–terram, diadema–

38\. tis–depictâ–veste, agitantem–universa–inferna arcus–nervi–sonitu, illam, regiones bracchiorum–millibus undique penetrando

39\. adstantem. Tunc processit pugna cum hac Devia et Deorum–hostium, armis–telis*que* multifariam emissis collustratae *erant* regiones–et spatium.

40\. giones–*et* spatium. Mahischi–Asuri–dux Tschikschus–nominatus, magnus–Asurus, dimicabat, Tschâmarus quoque cum aliis, exercitu–integro–praeditus.

41\. Curruum ayutis sex Udagrus–nominatus

42\. magnus–Asurus dimicabat ayutis*que* millenis Mahâhanus. Quinquaginta niyutis Asilomus magnus–Asurus, ayutis sexcentis

43\. Vâschkalus dimicabat in pugna. Ab elephantorum–equorum–copiis innumeris Ugradarsanus circumdatus curruum*que* kotî, in hac

44\. pugna dimicabat. Vidâlus–nominatus magnus–Daityus a quinquaginta tunc ayutis curribus dimicabat in proelio ibi circumdatus.

45\. Circumdatus *erat* Kâlus curruum in pugna quinquaginta–ayutis, alii quoque ibi ayutatim curribus–elephantis–equis circumdati dimicabant in pugna cum Devia ibi magni–Asuri.

46\. A kotium–kotium–millibus autem curruum elephantorum etiam equorumque

47\. circumdatus in pugna ibi erat Mahischus–Asurus. Vectibus–ferreis, parvis–sagittisque lanceis, pistillis quoque dimicabant in pugna cum

48\. Devia, ensibus, securibus–*et* telis. Alii etiam iaculati sunt lanceas alii funes alii etiam hanc Deviam ensium–ictibus occidere studue–

49\. runt. Ipsa etiam Devia Tschandica deinde haec arma *et* tela per

50\. lusum veluti fidit, sua–arma–tela*que*–effundens. Illaeso–vultu Devia laudata, a Diis–*et* sapientibus, dimisit in Asurorum–corpora

51\. tela armaque Domina. Ipse quoque iratus iubam–quassans Deviae vector leo ambulabat inter Asurorum–exercitus in sylvis sicuti

52\. Hutâsanus. Gemitus quos edidit dimicans in pugna Ambica hi

53\. etiam subito congregati *sunt* in catervas centeni–*et* milleni. Dimicabant hi securibus parvis sagittis–ensibus–*et* telis, delentes Asu–

54\. rorum–turbas Deviae–vi–repletas. Sonos ciebant tympanorum catervae, concharum quoque alii, parvorum–tympanorum etiam alii

55\. in hoc pugnae–magno–festo. Tunc Devia tridente clavâ hasta–

56\. rum–pluviis ense–aliisque centuriatim occidit magnos–Asuros; prostravit etiam alios tintinnabulorum–sonitu–perturbatos Asuros humi,

57\. fune ligatos alios abripuit. Quidam bipartiti facti sunt acutorum ensium–ictibus, alii quoque vulnerati ictu, clavâ, humi iacebant.

58\. Vomuerunt etiam alii sanguinem pistillo admodum laesi, alii prostrati

59\. humi *sunt* fissi hastâ in pectore. Continua–sagittarum–copia dissecati quidam in loco–pugnae, pallentes animas exhalarunt Deorum–

60\. vexatores. Quorundam brachia fissa *erant,* fissi–cervicibus *erant* quoque alii, capita ceciderunt aliorum, alii in medio *erant* dissecati.

61\. Dissecati–cruribus autem alii deciderunt in terram magni–Asuri,

62\. uno–brachio–oculo–pede alii a Devia bipartiti facti *sunt.* Fisso–que etiam alii capite delapsi, rursus erecti, trunci dimicarunt cum Devia capientes–eximia–arma, saltaruntque alii ibi in pugna instru–

63\. mentorum–*musicorum* numerum–sequentes. Trunci, fissi–capitibus, enses–hastas–gladios–in manibus–gestabant; ,,sta, sta!'' ita

64\. allocuti *sunt* Deviam alii magni–Asuri. Prostratis curribus–elephantis–equis Asurisque terra difficilis–accessu erat ubi erat

65\. illa magna–pugna. Sanguinis–copiae, magna–flumina subito ibi fluxerunt in medio Asurorum–exercitu inter elephantos–Asuros–

*66. et* equos. Statim illum magnum–exercitum Asurorum etiam Ambica ad exitium dedit, sicuti ignis graminis–*et* ligni–magnam–



67\. copiam. Ipse quoque leo magnum–strepitum emittens, iubam quassans, e corporibus immortalium–hostium–spiritûs–quasi quae–

68\. sivit. Cum Devia catervisque his ibi commissa–est pugna similiter Asuris, ita ut illam laudarent Dii florum–pluviam–effundentes in coelo.

**—————**

**CANTUS III.**

**———**

**Sapiens dixit:**

1\. Occisum hunc exercitum cum vidisset magnus–Asurus exercitus–dux

2\. Tschikschurus, iratus ivit dimicatum deinde Ambicâm. Hic Deviam sagittarum–pluviâ obruit in pugna Asurus, sicut Meruis–montis

3\. cacumen aquae–pluviâ nubes. Huius findens deinde Devia per lusum quasi sagittarum–fasciculos, occidit equos sagittis aurigamque

4\. equorum. Fiditque arcum subito vexillumque alte–sublatum, fe–

5\. riit quoque membra fissum–arcum *habentis* sagittis. Hic fisso–arcu, sine–curru, occisis–equis, occiso–auriga irruit *in* ipsam Deviam,

6\. ensem–scutum–gestans Asurus. Leonem feriens ensis acuta–acie in capite, vulneravit in bracchio sinistro Deviam quoque celerrimus.

7\. Huius ensis bracchium cum accederet, ruptus est, o principis–fili,

8\. tunc cepit hastam ille irâ ruber–oculis. Coniecitque deinde hancce in Bhadrakâliam magnus–Asurus fulgentem splendoribus solis–orbis

9\. veluti de coelo. Videns hanc advolantem hastam Devia hastam emisit, istius–hasta in centum–partes ab hac fracta *est* ipseque ma–

10\. gnus–Asurus. Occiso hoc pervalido Mahischi exercitus–duce, ac–

11\. cessit elephanto–vectus Tschâmarus, Deorum–vexator. Is quoque hastam coniecit deinde in Deviam, hanc Ambica celeriter incan–

12\. tatione–ictam, humi prostravit splendoris–expertem. Fractam hastam *et* prostratam cum vidisset, irâ–commotus iaculatus est Tschâ–

13\. marus hastam, sagittis hanc quoque illa fidit. Deinde leo exsi–liens, inter–elephanti–frontis–globulos stans brachiis pugnabat

14\. cum illo alte Deorum–hoste. Dimicantes tunc ambo, ab hoc elephanto in terram descendentes, certabant valde–furentes, icti–

15\. bus perhorrendis. Deinde celeriter in aëra exsiliendo subsiliendoque ab animalium–hoste, pedis–motu caput Tschâmari ab–

16\. scissum *est.* Udagrus*que* in pugna a Devia lapidibus–arboribus–*et* aliis occisus *est* et dentibus–pugnis–*et* pedibus item Karâlus

17\. prostratus *est.* Devia irata clavarum–ictibus confregit surgentem 18. Vâschcalum, parvo–telo sagittis Tâmrum item Andhacum. Ugrâsyum, Ugraviryum perinde atque Mahâhanum triops tridente oc–

19\. cidit summa–domina. Vidâlasyi ense de corpore decussit caput, Durdharum Durmukhumque, ambo sagittis abduxit in Yami–sedem.

20\. Ita exstincto suo–exercitu Mahischus–Asurus bubuli suâ–formâ

21\. perterruit illas catervas. Alios capitis–ictu, ungularum–ictibus item alios, caudâ–percussosque alios cornibusque dilaceratos, ce–

22\. leritate quosdam, alios strepitu agitation*eque,* spiritus–vento alios

23\. prostravit humi. Conciso Sivi–exercitu, accurrebat ipse Asurus ad

24\. leonem occidendum magnae–Deae, irata est tum Ambica. Iste quoque irâ pervalidus, ungulis–contundens–terram, cornibus montes

25\. altos vibravit strepitumque edidit. Celeri–agitatione–contrita terra

26\. dehiscebat istius caudâ, ictumque mare fluctuabat undique. Agitatis–cornibus–divisae in diversas partes abierunt nubes, spiritus–vento–

27\. icti centuriatim deciderunt ex aëre montes. Ita irâ–inflatum, irruentem magnum–Asurum videns, ipsa Tschandica irata est ad

28\. istum–occidendum tunc. Ipsa iniiciens huic compedem, eum constrinxit magnum–Asurum, deseruit bubuli formam iste quoque li–

29\. gatus in magna–pugna. Deinde leo factus est statim, quamdiu

30\. huius Ambica caput fidit, tamdiu vir ensifer conspiciebatur. Tunc quoque celeriter virum Devia fidit sagittis eum ense–*et* scuto *ar–*

31\. *matum;* deinde iste factus est magnus–elephas. Proboscideque magnum–leonem illum abripuit et vociferatus est, abripientis autem

32\. proboscidem Devia ense abscidit. Tunc magnus–Asurus iterum bubuli corpus assumsit atque agitabat trimundum cum–mobili–

33\. bus–*et* immobilibus. Deinde irata mundi–mater Tschandica po–tum optimum bibit, iterum iterumque etiam risit torvo–vultu.

34\. Sonum ediditque Asurus ille etiam ingentis–roboris–ebrietate–ex–

35\. citatus cornibusque coniecit in Tschandicam montes. Ipsaque hos coniectos ab isto confringens sagittarum–copiis, allocuta est illum ebrietate–excitatum, vultus–rubore–turbatum–oculis.

**Devia dixit:**

36\. ,,Clama, clama aliquantulum o stulte! potum dum bibo ego, a me ,,te te occiso, heic etiam clamabunt cito Dii.''

**Sapiens dixit:**

37\. Sic locuta exsiliens illa conscendit istum magnum–Asurum, pede–

38\. que imposito gulae, hastâ eum percussit. Deinde iste, etiamsi pede–conculcatus ab illa, e suo–corpore tunc semi–egressus quoque

39\. vehementer a Deviae robore tectus *est.* Semi–egressus quoque iste dimicans magnus–Asurus ab illa Devia magno–ense, capite fisso,

40\. prostratus *est.* Deinde eheu, eheu! clamabatur, omnis Daityorum–exercitus periit ille, gaudiumque summum nacti sunt omnes

41\. Deorum–catervae. Laudabant illam Suri Deviam cum coelestibus magnis–sapientibus, cantabant Gandharvorum–domini, saltabantque Apsarasarum–catervae.

**—————**

**CANTUS IV.**

**———**

**Sapiens dixit:**

1\. Sacrus–*et* reliquae deorum–catervae, occisis pervalido isto pravo et deorum–hostis–exercitu a Devia, hanc celebrabant veneratione–inclinatis–cervicibus–*et* humeris, hymnis, *catervae* prae gaudio–pilorum–arrectione–pulchris–corporibus *praeditae.*



**Dei dixerunt:**

2\. A qua Deviâ, expansus *est* hic mundus ipsius–vi omnium–Deorum–catervarum–virium–coniunctione–formatâ, huic Ambicae, ab omnibus–Diis–*et* magnis–sapientibus–venerandae, veneratione incli–

3\. nati nos *sumus,* tribuat salutem illa nobis! Cuius potentiam incomparabilem almus Anantus, Brahmus Harusque ne eloqui quidem valent, haecce Tschandica ad universi–mundi–conservationem

4\. interitumque calamitatis–timoris consilium capiat. Quae fortuna ipsa *es* piorum in originibus, adversa fortuna impiorum, in sapientum cordibus intellectus, fides bonorum, nobili–familiâ–exorti pudor, huic tibi inclinati nos *sumus,* tuere, o Devia universum!

5\. Quid describamus tuam formam incogitabilem illam, quid etiam magnam–fortitudinem, Asurorum–caedem–efficientem omnino, quid etiam facinora tua admirabilia in omnibus, o Devia, Asurorum–

6\. *et* Deorum–catervarum–*et* aliorum proeliis. Causa *es* omnium–mundorum; tribus–qualitatibus *praedita,* tamen cum vitiis non cognosceris, Hare–Haro–*et* reliquis excelsior, *tu es* omnium–refugium, universus hicce mundus tui–pars *est,* increata enim *es,* summa, na–

7\. tura, tu *es* prima. Quam omnes–Dei effando gaudium adipiscuntur in omnibus sacrificiis, o Devia, Swâha es et patrum–catervae gaudii–causa, pronuntiaris tu inde etiam ab hominibus Swadha etiam.

8\. *Tu* quae *es* beatitudinis–causa, haud–cogitabile–magnis–votis quoque *praedita* veneraris ab admodum–coercitis–sensibus–veritatis–essentiam–adeptis, a beatitudinis–cupidis, a sapientibus, omnia–vitia–deiicientibus; scientia es ipsa Bhagavatia, summa enim *es* o Devia!

9\. Soni–naturâ–induta *es,* perpuri–Ritsch–*et* Yadschus thesaurus et Udgithi–*veluti* iucundis–metris–lectorum hymnorum; o Devia! *tu es* Trayia, Bhagavatia, affer salutem, *tu es* nutrimentum omnium–mun–

10\. dorum *et* summa doloris–deletrix. Prudentia es, o Devia! intellectam–omnium–scientiarum–essentiam *habens,* Durga es, calamitatis–oceani–navis, non–adstricta, Fortuna, in Kaitabhi–hostis (Vischnuis)–corde–sola–habitans, tu *es* Gauria utique lunae–diademate–

11\. factam–gloriam *habens. Etsi* paulum ridentem puram plenilunii–orbis–similitudinem *habente*–auri–optimi–splendore–pulchram miri–ficam faciem conspiciebat, nihilominus a Mahischo–Asuro irâ–incenso

12\. subito pugnatum *est.* Intuens autem, O Devia, iratam, superciliorum–contractione–terribilem, orientis–lunae–splendori–similem (*faciem*), quod *tum* non subito animam efflarit Mahischus, hoc valde

13\. mirum; quibus enim vita restat irati–Antaci–conspectu? O Devia fave! summa tu ipsa *es* saluti, subito deles iracunda familias, perceptum hoc nunc *est,* cum ad ruinam ille ductus *sit* exercitus per–

14\. magnus Mahischi–Asuri. A te honoratis in terra, divitiae *sunt* his, his *sunt* honores, nec perit officiorum–ordo; divites ii etiam gratis–filiis–servis–*et* uxore *praediti,* quibus semper fortunas–dans tu

15\. ipsa favens *es.* Religiosa, O Devia, omnia semper certe officia intente quotidie pius perficit, in coelum pervenitque deinde tuo–ipsius–favore, nonne in trimundo etiam, fructum–das, o Devia,

16\. ideo? In periculo implorata deles metum omnibus–animantibus, a prosperis implorata consilium valde eximium das, O paupertaten–dolorem–metum–delens, quae, praeter te alia, omnibus–mu–

17\. tuis–officiis–praestandis semper madido–animo *praedita est?* His occisis mundus nanciscitur voluptatem, similiter ipsi perpetrent item peccatum *quod* ad Tartarum diuturnum *ducit,* in proelio–mortem perpessi in coelum perveniant; cogitans ita certe hostes de–

18\. les, O Devia! Intuens quidni tu ipsa vertis in cinerem omnes–Asuros? in hostes cum mittas tela, ad mundos enim accedant hostes etiam telis–lustrati, hoc modo consilium est erga istos inimicos

19\. bonum. Ensium–splendoris–copiae–vibrationibus etiam horrendis, hastarum–cuspidum–fulgoris–multitudine, oculi Asurorum quod non adierunt ruinam, *quia* fulgentis–lunae–parti–similem–vultum tuum

20\. videbant hoc est *factum.* Sceleratorum–vitae–inhibitio tuum *est,* O Devia, ingenium; forma quoque haec haud–cogitanda, incomparabilis cum aliis; roburque *est* interficiens *eos qui* delent–deorum–fortitudinem, erga hostes etiam manifestata *est* misericor–

21\. dia a te ita. Quocum similitudo sit tuae huius fortitudinis, formaque hostium–metum–efficiens, valde rapiens, ubi? in animo misericordia, in pugna–asperitas etiam visa *est* in te quoque, O De–

22\. via, gratiam–dans in trimundo etiam. Trimundus hic universusab hostium–deletione servatus *est* per te, in proelii–fronte *dum* tu quoque occidis, ductae *sunt* in coelum hostium–catervae, metus etiam abiectus noster furentibus–deorum–hostibus–exortus, adoratio *sit*

23\. tibi! Hastâ tuere nos, o Devia! tuere ense etiam, o Ambica, tin–

24\. tinnabuli–sono nos tuere, arcus–nervi–stridore quoque. In oriente serva, in occidente etiam, o Tschandica, serva in meridie, vibratione

25\. tuae ipsius–hastae in septentrione item o Domina! Quae pulchrae formae in trimundo incedunt tuae, et quae supra–modum–

26\. horrendae *sunt,* his serva nos, item*que* terram. Ensis–hasta–clava–*et* alia quae tua *sunt* arma, o Ambica! in manus–ramo–coniuncta, his nos serva omnino.

**Sapiens dixit:**

27\. Ita celebrata a Deis, coelestibus floribus Nandano–exortis culta

28\. mundorum–servatrix, similiter odoribus–*et* unctionibus; religiose ab omnibus Diis suffimentis coelestibus fumigata, allocuta est favore–placida–facie omnes inclinatos Deos.

**Devia dixit:**

29\. Eligant Dii omnes, quod*cunque* a me desideratur dabo ego perlubenter, laudibus hisce admodum–honorata.

**Dei dixerunt:**

30\. Ab excelsa peractum *est* omne, haud quicquam restat, cum iste

31\. occisus *sit* hostis noster Mahischus–Asurus. Quodsi vero etiam gratia danda *est* a te nobis, o magna–domina! implorata, implorata

32\. tu nostras deleas summas–calamitates! Quique mortalis laudibus hisce te celebrabit, o purâ–facie *praedita!* huic facultatibus–divitiis–opibus, incremento e divitiis–uxore–*et* reliquis *compositae* felicitatis nobis–favens *(i. e. nostra causa)* tu sis omnino, o Ambica!

**Sapiens dixit:**

33\. Ita ad favorem excitata a Diis mundi causa atque ipsius, ,,esto''

34\. ita cum dixisset Bhadracâlia, evanuerat, o rex! Ita hoc expositum*est,* o princeps! exorta illa quomodo olim *erat* Devia e Deorum–

36\. similiter Sumbhi–*et* Nisumbhi, ad conservationemque mundorum, Deorum auxiliatrix, hoc audi a me, expositum sicuti, enarrabo tibi.

47\. rorum-domine! Feminarum-margarita, perpulchris-membris col-lustrans regiones; splendore ipsa stat, o Daityorum-rex, hanc te

48\. videre oportet. Quae res-pretiosae, gemmae, elephanti-equi-*et* alia, o insignis! in trimundo *existunt*, *haec* universa nunc fulgent

50\. militer Utschtschaisravus equus. Vehiculum anseribus-iunctum illud stat in tuo atrio egregium, admirabile *quod* huc adductum

53\. eximius qui olim erat animantium-domino. Mortis superatrix vide-licet lancea, domine, a te capta *est*; vinculum aquae-regis in fratris

54\. tui custodia *est*. Nisumbho *sunt* ex oceano-procreata omnia gem-marum-genera; Vahnis etiam dedit tibi duas igne-purificatas vestes.

58\. que accedat lubenter, *id* ita efficiendum a te facile. Hic postquam eo iverat, quo commorabatur in montana-regione valde-amoena, hanc Deviam deinde allocutus est suave mellita voce.

Nuntius dixit:

59\. O Devia! Daityorum-dominus Sumbhus in trimundo summus-princeps *est*, nuntius ego missus ab hoc coram-te heic profectus *sum*.

63\. ,,phantorum etiam captus *est,* Dei-Indri-vector. E lactis-oceani-,,agitatione-exorta equorum-margarita mea *est,* Utschtschaisravus-,,cognominatus, ab immortalibus veneratione exhibita hic creatus *est*.

65\. ,,existunt, haec mihi sunt, o splendida! Feminarum-margaritam,,te, o Devia! in mundo putamus nos, ipsa tu ad nos accede, quia

66\. ,,margaritarum-cultores nos *sumus.* Me, aut meum fratrem-mino-,,rem etiam Nisumbhum ingenti-fortitudine-*praeditum* cole tu, va-,,cillantibus oculi-angulis *instructa!* cum profecto margarita sis.

71\. diatur a te imprudente votum quod factum sit olim. ,,Qui ,,me devincit in pugna, qui meam superbiam supprimit, qui mei

72\. ,,similis-vi *est* in mundo, is meus maritus erit." Quare accedat Sumbhus huc Nisumbhusve magnus-Asurus, me devicta, confestim certe manum capiet meam facile.

73\. Superba es, ne ita tu, o Devia, loquere me coram, in trimundo

74\. quis vir stet coram Sumbho-*et* Nisumbho? Reliquis etiam Daityis omnes Dii non in proelio resistunt adverso ore, o Devia,

76\. *et* reliquos femina procedas adverso ore? Ipsa tu accedas, a me etiam compellata, ad Sumbhum-et Nisumbhum ne capillorum-attractu-deiecta-gravitate venias.

78\. Ipse tu abeas, a me dictum tibi quod *est*, hoc omne cum vene-ratione enarra Asurorum-principi, isque quod aptum *videatur,* faciat.

12\. sius-vector. Quosdam ungularum-ictu Daityos, vultuque alios, proterendo quoque deorsum alios occidit celeriter magnos-Asuros.

15\. iubam. Statim ille exercitus universus exstinctus *est* a magnanimo

16\. illo leone, Deviae vectore perirato. Audiens illum Asurum a Devia occisum Dhûmralotschanum, exercitumque deletum universum

17\. a Deviae-leone deinde; iratus est Daityorum-princeps Sumbhus trementibus-labiis, mandata deditque ambobus Tschando-*et* Mun-

Sapiens dixit:

15\. que. Confestim illum exercitum universum Asurorum prostratum

19\. intus horrendis-visu-dentibus-fulgens. Conscendens etiam magnum-leonem Devia in Tschandum irruit, prehensumque eius ca-

20\. pillis caput, illo ense fidit. Tum Mundus quoque irruit in eam, intuens Tschandum prostratum, illum etiam irâ prostravit humi

24.,,Nisumbhumque occides." Illos adductos deinde conspiciens Tschandum-*et* Mundum, magnos-Asuros, dixit Kâliae, eximia

17\. forma-praedita. Similiter etiam Vischnuis Vis, Garudo-insistens, concham-discum-clavam-arcum Vischnuis-*et* ensem-gerens accessit.

20\. stellarum-agmen. Fulmen-gestans similiter Aindria elephantorum-rege-insistens accessit, oculorum-millibus *praedita* sicut Sacrus ipsa

29\. processere quo Kâtyâyania stabat. Tunc primum coram *illa* sa-gittarum-hastarum-ensium-pluviis obruebant irâ- tumentes illam De-

30\. viam immortalium-hostes. Ipsa quoque has emissas sagittas, hastas-discos-*et* secures dissecavit iocans stridente- arcu-solutis

31\. magnis-sagittis. Prope eam deinde Kâlia hastarum-ictibus-di-laceratos, clâva-vulneratos etiam hostes efficiens, incedebat tum.

33\. titudine Brahmânia effecit hostes, quocunque cucurrit. Mâhesvaria tridente, similiter disco Vaischnavia Daityos occidit, Kaumâria

34\. utique hastâ, irata. Aindriae fulminis-ictu centeni Daityi-*et* Da-

35\. navi cecidere dilacerati humi, sanguinis-copiam-effundentes. Oris-impetu-laesi, dentibus-acutis-vulnerati-pectoribus, Apriformis con-

36\. cidere disco etiam dilacerati. Unguibus dilaceratos etiam alios devorans magnos-Asuros, Nârasinhia incedebat in pugna, sonitu-

37\. implens-regiones-*et* spatium. Terribilibus-cachinnis Asuri a Sivadûtia-laesi cecidere humi, lapsos hos comedit deinde illa tum.

38\. Ita matrum-catervam iratam conterentem magnos-Asuros cum vi-

39\. disset, variis modis periere Deorum-hostium-copiae. Fugae-de-ditos cum vidisset Daityos matrum-catervâ-vexatos pugnatum irruit

40\. iratus Ractavidschus magnus-Asurus. Sanguinis-’gutta quando in terram decidit ex eius corpore, exsilit e terra ipsi-similis tunc Asu-

41.rus. Dimicabat hic clavam-manu-gerens cum Indri-Vi magnus-Asurus, tunc etiam Aindria suo-fulmine Ractavidschum vulneravit.

42\. Fulmine icti celeriter huius profluxit sanguis, exsiliere deinde pu-

43\. gnatores istius-formà, istius-fortitudine *praediti*. Quot decidere ex eius corpore sanguinis-guttae, tot viri orti *sunt*, istius-fortitu-

44\. dine-vi-*et* robore instructi. Hi quoque dimicabant ibi viri san-guine exorti cum matribus perduro telorum-vibratione-horrendo

45\. modo. Iterumque cum fulminis-ictu vulneratum *esset* eius caput,

46\. effudit sanguinem, viri*que* tunc procreati *sunt* milleni. Vaischnavia in pugna etiam illum disco feriit, clavâ vulneravit Aindria hunc

47\. Asurorum-dominum. Vaischnaviae-disco-fissi sanguinis-effusione-exortis, millenis mundus penetratus *est* illi-similibus magnis-Asuris.

48\. Hastâ vulneravit Kaumâria, Apriformis similiter ense, Mâhesvaria

49\. tridente Ractavidschum magnum-Asurum. Ipse quoque clavâ Daityus omnes etiam feriit singulas utique matres, irâ-repletus

50\. Ractavidschus magnus-Asurus. Huius vulnerati multifariam hastâ-lanceâ *et* aliis, humi decidit quae sanguinis-copia, ex hac exstitere

51\. centeni Asuri. His etiam Asurorum-sanguine-exortis Asuris universus mundus penetratus erat, deinde Dii metum adibant summum.

52\. Hos perterritos Deos conspiciens, Tschandica dixit benignissime *et*

53\. affata est Kâliam: ,,O Tschamunda, os expande, meorum-telo-,,rum-ictibus-exortas sanguinis-guttas, magnos-Asuros, e sanguinis-

54\. ,,gutta absorbe tu ore hocce celeriter." Devorans incede in pugna ab-illo procreatos magnos-Asuros, ita ille in exitium Dait-

55\. yus, sanguine-deleto vocabit. Devoratis a te horrendis, alii etiam haud exorientur, ita allocuta illam tunc Devia lanceâ vulne-

56\. ravit illum. Ore Kâlia excepit Ractavidschi sanguinem, deinde

57\. hic feriit tunc clavâ ibi Tschandicam. Neque illi dolorem effecit clavae-ictus minimum quoque, ipsum etiam feriit Devia clavâ im-

58\. probum. Ex huius vulnerati corpore autem multum profluxit san-

59\. guinis huc et illuc, hunc ore Tschâmunda absorpsit. Ex illius ore qui egrediebantur sanguine-decidente magni-Asuri, hos devo-

60\. ravit tunc Tschâmunda bibitque eorum sanguinem. Devia, hastâ fulmine sagittis ensibus gladiis occidit Ractavidschum illum, cuius-

61\. sanguinem-biberat-Tschâmunda. Hic decidit in terram supinus, telorum-copiâ-vulneratus, exsanguis quoque *erat*, o terrae-custos,

62\. Ractavidschus magnus-Asurus. Deinde illi gaudium summum nacti sunt tredecim, o rex; occiso isto matrum-caterva saltabat sanguine-inebriata.

**CANTUS IX.  
————**

Rex dixit:

1\. Admirabilis haecce exposita, o excelse! a te mihi Deviae rerum

2\. gestarum-maiestas ad Ractavidschi-caedem-pervenit. Ulterius quoque cupio ego audire, quid, Ractavidscho occiso, Sumbhus fe-cerit, Nisumbhusque valde iratus.

Sapiens dixit:

3\. Iratus est magnopere, Ractavidscho occiso, Sumbhus-Asurus Ni-

4\. sumbhusque, occisis reliquis quoque in pugna. Occisum magnum-exercitum cum vidisset, iram emittens irruit Nisumbhus tunc cum

5\. excellentissimo Asurorum-exercitu. Huius a fronte itemque a tergo et lateribus magni-Asuri collidentes-labia-superiora, irati

6\. occisum Deviam aggressi sunt. Accessit pervalidus Sumbhus quo-que a suis-copiis circumdatus occisum Tschandicam ex ira, post-

7\. quam pugnarat cum Matribus. Deinde proelium grave erat De-viae Sumbhi-Nisumbhique, sagittarum-pluviam valde-horribilem

8\. nubium veluti effundentium. Fidit emissas sagittas ab his Tschandica ipsius-sagittarum-fasciculis, percussitque membra telorum-co-

9\. piis Asurorum-principum. Nisumbhus acutum ensem scutumque sustulit persplendidum *et* vulneravit in capite leonem Deviae ve-

10\. ctorem eximium. Vulnerato vectore Devia, sagittâ-pedis-equi *formam* *gerente* gladium eximium Nisumbhi celeriter fidit scutumque

12\. verso-irruentem. Irâ-incensus Nisumbhus tunc hastam arripuit

14\. Deviae tridente fissa, in cinerem versa *est.* Deinde securim-manu-ferentem illum irruentem Daityorum-optimum, vulneravit De-

15\. via sagittarum-copiis et prostravit humi. Hoc prostrato humi Nisumbho terribili-fortitudine ob fratrem valde iratus progressus est

17\. fulgebat coelum. Hunc accedentem intuens Devia, concham infla-

18\. vit, nervi-sonum etiam arcus effecit difficillimum-toleratu. Implevit regiones propriorum-tintinnabulorum-sonitu, omnium-Daityo-

22\. census est irâ. Cum ,,improbe, sta, sta!" ita clamasset Ambica,

24\. iecta *est*. Leonino-rugitu Sumbhi repletus est trimundus-*et* in-teriectum spatium, venti impetus-strepitus horribilis exortus *est*, o

25\. terrae-princeps! A Sumbho-missas sagittas Devia, Sumbhus ab hac-emissas sagittas fidit suis-sagittis horrendis centenis atque mil-

26\. lenis. Deinde ipsa Tschandica irata hastâ percussit eum; is tunc

28\. leonem. Iterumque procreans brachiorum ayutum Danue-nato-

** CANTUS X.  
————**

Sapiens dixit:

1\. Nisumbhum occisum videns fratrem vitae-instar-dilectum, prostra-

2\. tumque exercitum Sumbhus iratus dixit: ,,Fortitudinis-superbiâ, ,,o tu prava Durga! ne superbam te praebeas, aliarum fortitudine ,,assumpta dimicas admodum-arrogans."

Devia dixit:

3\. Sola profecto ego in mundo *sum*, heic altera praeter me quae alia? conspice illas, o stulte, in me intrantes, meas-evolutiones!

Sapiens dixit:

4\. Deinde omnes illae Deae Brahmânia-duce facile huius Deviae cor pus ingressae sunt; sola certe erat tunc Ambica.

Devia dixit:

5\. Ego evolutione in multis heic formis quod (i. e. qualis) praesens *sum*, id inclusum est in me, sola certe adsto, in pugna firmus esto!

Sapiens dixit:

6\. Tunc versabatur pugna terribilis, amborum Deviae et Sumbhi, in-

7\. tuentibus omnibus-Diis Asurisque. Sagittarum-imbribus acutis telis, itemque armis horrendis horum exstitit porro pugna, omni-

8\. bus-mundis-timorem-inferens. Coelestia tela quae Ambica de-inde centena dimisit, fregit haec Daityorum-princeps per illis-ad-

9\. versos ictus. Emissa ab illa quoque tela coelestia, summa-Domina fregit per lusum certe durum in modum incantationibus-*et* aliis.

10\. Tunc sagittarum-centuriis Deviam operuit iste Asurus, ipsa quoque

11\. de isto-irata Devia arcum fidit sagittis. Fisso arcu Daityorum-princeps tunc hastam sustulit, fidit Devia disco hanc in eius manu.

12\. Deinde ensem tollens centum-lunis *ornatum* et splendidum, irruit

13\. deinde in Deviam Daityorum princeps. Huius irruentis etiam celeriter ensem fidit Tschandica arcu-missis acutis sagittis, scutum-

14\. que solis-radii-*veluti* fulgens. Equosque prostravit *et* currum cum auriga, occisis- equis hic *erat* tunc Daityus, fisso-arcu *et* sine-auriga;

15\. arripuit malleum terribilem ad Ambicae-exitium-paratus, fidit ir-ruentis huius malleum emissis sagittis; nihilominus accurrit ad il-

16\. lam capulum emittens celeriter. Is capulum iniecit cordi Daityorum-optimus Deviae, hunc etiam ipsa Devia plantâ-pedis in pe-

17\. ctore vulneravit, plantae pedis-ictu-percussus concidit in terram;

18\. hic Daityorum-rex celeriter iterum etiam exsurrexit. Cum exsi-luisset et arripuisset sursum Deviam, in aëra se erexit; heic quo-que illa sine-fundo (i. e. terra haud insistens) dimicavit cum isto

19\. Tschandica, pugnam in aëre tunc Daityus et Tschandica mutuo, dimicabant egregiam pugnam sapientum-admirationem-excitantem.

20\. Deinde pugnâ perdiu pugnatâ cum illo Ambica abripiens *eum*

21\. conquassavit *et* deiecit in terram; iste deiectus in terram, nactus capulum sustulit celeriter *et* irruit, pravo-animo Tschandicae-exi-

22\. tium-cupiens; hunc accedentem deinde Devia omnium-Daityo-

23\. rum-gentium-principem humi prostravit, pectore hastâ fisso. Is exanimis decidit in terram Deviae-hastae-cuspide-vulneratus, agitans universam terram cum-maribus-*et* insulis, *et* cum-montibus.

24\. Deinde quietum *erat* universum occiso hoc improbo, mundus sa-

25\. lutem summam nactus est, serenumque erat coelum; portento-sae-nubes cum-meteoris igneis quae antea exstiterant, hae sunt tranquillatae, flumina cursum-sequentia etiam erant, illo occiso.

26\. Tunc Deorum-catervae omnes *prae* gaudio-allevatis-animis erant,

27\. occiso hoc, Gandharvi*que* laeta cecinerunt; cantabant etiam alii, saltaruntque Apsarasarum-catervae, flabant puri etiam venti, persplendidus erat sol, fulgebant quoque ignes placati sedatis-regionibus exortis-sonis *praediti.*

Sapiens dixit:

46\. in terra. Ibique occidam Durgamum-nominatum magnum-Asu-

47\. rum, Durgae Deae ita illustre illud mihi nomen erit. Iterumque quando, horrenda forma assumpta, in nivis-monte Racschasos ego

48\. devorabo sapientium conservationis-causa; tunc me sapientes omnes laudabunt *veneratione* inclinatis-corporibus; Horrendae Deae

49\. ita illustre illud mihi nomen erit. Quando Arunus-nominatus in trimundo magnam-caedem perficit, tunc ego circumvagantem for-

50\. mam assumens ex innumeris-apibus compositam, trimundi salutis-causa occidam magnum-Asurum, Circumvagantem (Apem) ita me ho-

51\. mines tunc celebrabunt omnino. Hoc modo quando malum Dânavis-exortum erit, tunc descendens ego perficiam hostium-caedem.

————

**CANTUS XII.**

———

Devia dixit:

1\. Hisce laudibus qui me semper enixe praedicabit, huius ego omnem

2\. sollicitudinem sedabo, sine dubio. Madhuis-*et* Kaitabhi-interitum atque Mahischi-Asuri-caedem itemque Sumbhi-*et* Nisumbhi exci-

3\. dium qui celebrabunt, octavo, decimo-quarto et nono die in unum animo-intenti qui audibunt utique religiose meam praecla-

4\. ram maiestatem; his non ullum male-factum nec ex malefacto-exorta calamitas erit, nec paupertas, nec optati-frustratio.(13)

5\. Non ab hoste vel fure, vel rege, non ab-telorum-ignium-aqua-

6\. rum-copia unquam metus illi exorietur. Propterea haecce mea maiestas perlegenda ab intentis audiendaque semper religiose; sum-

7. ma enim haec est salutis-via. Omnia praesagia autem ex Mahâmâria-exorta, similiter triplex prodigium maiestas coerceat

8\. mea. Ubi haec recte semper legitur in ara mea, nunquam hanc

9\. relinquam, ibique praesentia est mea. In sacrificiis, in cultu, in ignibus-sacris, in magno festo, universa haec mea historia enuntianda

10\. atque audienda est. A gnaro ignarove sacrificium-victimae insti-

11\. tutum lubenter exspecto similiter ignis-sacrificium. Quae sacra anniversaria auctumno celebrantur, in his qui (devotione) religione-

12\. instructus hanc meam audit maiestatem, *is* homo meo-favore ab omni-sollicitudine-liberatus, divitiis-oryzâ-filiis-praeditus erit, sine

13\. dubio. Hac mea maiestate similiter originibus praeclaris audi-

14\. tis atque fortitudine in pugnis, impavidus exoritur homo. Hostes intereunt, fausta prodeunt, gaudetque familia hominum meam ma-

15\. iestatem audientium. In omni placandi-actione similiter in somni-difficilis somniis et in spectrorum-tormentis duris, ma-

16\. iestatem audiat meam. Portenta et spectrorum-tormenta horrenda et difficilis quem homines sentiunt somnus, placantur, faci-

17\. lisque nascitur somnus. Infantium-daemonibus-oppressorum infantium lenimen, in turbae-dissensione quoque hominibus amicitiae

18\. causa est eximia. Impiorum omnium vim infirmans, summa dae-

19\. monum-spectrorum-lemurum lectione utique deletrix. Universa haec mea maiestas, me praebet-vicinam victimis-floribus-obla-

20\. tionibus-suffimentis atque odoratis-flammis similiter optimis. Brahmanorum cibis, sacrificiis, victimis-sacrificandis die-noctuque aliisque variis cibis, donis quovis anno, quod paratur mihi gaudium

21\. id affertur hac pulchra historia semel audita, audita delet peceatum itemque liberat a morbis, salutem praebet prae lemuribus

22\. originum mearum laudatio. Quia me auctore in pugnis pravi-Daityi-exstincti-sunt, hoc audito hostibus-natus timor hominibus

23\. haud oritur. Allatae a vobis a Brahmanicis-sapientibus et a

24\. Brahmo laudationes, hae eximium praebent consilium. In sylva, in loco deserto, a sylva-flagranti-circumfusus, sive in solitudine

25\. circumdatus a furibus, captusve quoque ab hostibus, a leone-*et* tigride-oppugnatus in sylva sive a sylvae-elephantibus, a crudeli rege iussus, occidendus, sive vinculis quoque constrictus;

26\. agitatusve a vento, in navicula stans in magno-mari, sive telis

27\. volantibus in praelio valde-horrendo, in omnibus-aerumnis terribilibus, sive doloribus-vexatus etiam, meam hancce historiam re-

28\. cordans homo ex angustiis liberatur. Mea potestate leones-*et* alia fures hostes*que* similiter e longinquo sane fugiunt meam historiam recordantes.

Sapiens dixit:

29\. Sic locuta ipsa sanctissima Tschandica, terribili-vi-instructa, Diis

30\. utique illic spectantibus, evanuit. Hi quoque Dii metu-vacantes, omnibus hostibus occisis, sicut (olim) antea munera-sua curabant,

31\. sacrificiorum-portionibus-fruentes. Daityi etiam, Sumbho Deorum-hoste a Devia in pugna deleto \* mundum-concutiente, perduro incomparabili-fortitudine-*praedito*, \* Nisumbho quoque per-

32\. valido omnes in Tartarum abiere. Talis est sanctissima Devia illa Sempiterna iterum iterumque etiam oriens, o rex! mundi sa-

33\. lutem perficit. Ab illa hoc universum conturbatur, ipsa certe universum producit, ipsa vocata cognitionem, *et* contenta divitias

34\. dat. Penetratur hoc universum Brahmi-ovum, o hominum princeps, ab illa Mahâkâlia, magno-tempore Mahâmâriae-formam ge-

35\. rente. Ipsa certe modo Mahâmâria ipsa profecto haud creata creatio est, stabilitatem animantium perficit, ipsa *est* modo Aeterna.

36\. Nascendi-tempore hominibus est Fortuna secunda, incrementum-praebens in familia, ipsa quoque moriendi-tempore similiter For-

37\. tuna-adversa ad perniciem exoritur. Laudata, culta floribus suffimentis-odoribus-*et* aliis etiam praebet divitias, filios similiter quoque in iure (religione) consilium praeclarum.

**CANTUS XIII.  
————**

Sapiens dixit:

1\. Haec tibi, o rex, narrata est Deviae-maiestas praeclara, talis-est

2\. potestas illius Deviae, a qua hic sustentatur mundus. Scientia similiter quoque efficitur excelsi-Vischnuis-magiâ; illâ tu ille Vaisyusque perinde quoque alii sapientes conturbantur, conturbati

3\. quoque in errorem incidunt etiam alii. Hanc aggredere, o magne-rex! tanquam refugium, summam-Dominam, culta ipsa ab hominibus voluptatem-coelum-et beatitudinem-dat.

Mârkandeyus dixit:

4\. Sic huius sermoue audito Surathus ille hominum-princeps, inclinando se *salutans* felicem hunc sapientem qui absolverat-vota.

5\. Liber a sui studio et regni-abrepti *memoria* se dedit subito de-

6\. votioni, illeque Vaisyus, o magne-sapiens! Conspiciendae-causa Ambae, in fluminis-insula-commorans, ille quoque Vaisyus, de-

7\. votionem exercebat Deviae-hymnum summum precans. Ambo in hac insula, Deviae ficta statua ex humo, colebant illam floribus-suf

8\. fimentis-igne-et aquae libationibus. Ieiunantes, parcum-cibum *comedentes,* in illam-defixi-animo, intenti praebebant victimam suo

9 rum-membrorum-sanguine-conspersam. Sic enixe colentibus per tres annos refraenatis-animis admodum-contenta mundi-servatrix coram *illis* dixit Tschandica.

Devia dixit:

10\. Quod desideratur a te o rex, a te etiam, o familiae-exhilarator! a me hoc desideretur, omne valde-contenta dabo hoc.

Mârkandeyus dixit:

11\. Deinde elegit princeps imperium securum in alia-nativitate, heic quoque proprium regnum *et* occisum-hostis-exercitum suo ipsius

12\. exercitu. Ille etiam Vaisyus tunc scientiam elegit liber-animo; mihi sit ita desiderium-delens *scientia*, ego sim sapiens.

Devia dixit:

13\. Paucis diebus, o princeps, tuum regnum adipisceris ipse, occisis

14\. hostibus, haud vacillans tibi *illud* deinde erit. Mortuusque porro adeptus nativitatem Deo Vivasvante, Sâvarnicus Manus nomen tibi

15\. in terra erit. Vaisyorum-eximie! a te quae gratia a me exoptata *est*, hanc dabo, ad perfectionem tuam scientia erit.

Mârkandeyus dixit:

16\. Sic tribuens ambobus Devia sicut-optarant gratiam, evanuerat sta-

17\. tim, religiose ab his laudata. Sic a Devia gratiam assecutus Surathus Kschatriyorum-optimus, a Sole nativitatem nactus, Sâvarnis erit Manus.

——————

**CANTUS I.**

Sl. 1. a. मनुः \। Secundum MAN. I. 61–63. septem, secundum BH. X. 6. quatuor et secundum Ham. et Langl. Cat. p. 56, 57. quatuordecim sunt Manues, quorum primus स्वयम्भू *per se ipsum-existens,* Brahmi filius MAN. VIII. 124. saepius autem idem ac Brahmus apparet; quodsi inter utrosque discernere velis, illum Manuem inter creatorem Brahmum et mundum interpositum putare possis. Ex aliis locis ea Brahmi et Manuis ratio patet, ut ille mundi omniumque rerum sit creator atque conditor, hic autem moderator atque princeps omnium ad spiritum et mentem humanam spectantium rerum, RAM. SER. III. 77. 4, 5., hanc ob causam homines appellantur मनुजाः *Manue-nati*. Praeter mentem et spiritum ipsum etiam omnes quae ad hominum salutem exoriuntur institutiones, Manui tribuuntur. Ex hac ethico-spirituali significatione legum corpus, a Brahmo ipso conditum, per Manuem hominibus promulgatum est. Appellatur Manus आदिराज *primus-rex,* RAM. SCHL. I. 6. 4. मानवेन्द्र *hominum-princeps* ibid. I. 6. 19. वैवस्वत *Vivasvantis* (*Solis*) *filius*, qui auctor est novae post diluvium creationis; DILUV. v. 51, 55. RAM. SER. III. 77. 4, 5. प्रजापति *animantium-dominus* ibid.

Sl. 2. a. मन्वन्तराधिपः। ad verbum: *Manuis-aetatis-princeps.* Naturae sive mundi existentia ex Indorum notionibus diversis magnis aetatibus vel temporis intervallis (अन्तर) completur, quorum cuilibet praeesse Manuem moderatorem putant, hinc मन्वन्तर usurpatur. Innumerae existunt tales Manuis aetates (मन्वन्तराणि) MAN. I. 80. Nam Indi hac opinione studebant corrigere falsum illud, quod inest finitae isti cogitandi rationi qua rerum initium statuebant, quamquam hac re vitium illud obtectum potius quam sublatum esse facile apparet. Praeterea, si accuratius inquiris, quatuor statuunt aetates, (युग) scilicet कृत, त्रेता, द्वापर et कलि MAN. I. 86. Depravationem deinceps apparentem hac ratione describunt, ut religionis et veritatis genium, qui formam bovis gerit MAN. VIII. 16. paullatim dìcant pedibus privari, ita ut initio, quattuor, deinde tribus tunc duobus denique uno pede insistat.

Sl. 3. a. स्वारोचिषेऽन्तरे। hoc est aetas cui स्वारोचिः, *secundus Manus,* praeest; reliquorum Manuum nomina haec sunt उत्तमि, तामस, रैवत, चाक्षुष, वैवस्वत. MAN. I. 62.

Sl. 4. b. तथा। B. तदा.

Sl. 7. a. आमात्यैर्। B et C. अमात्यैर्.

Sl. 9. a. द्विजवर्यस्य मेधसः। B द्विजवर्यः सुमेधसः

Sl. 11. a. ममत्व। Vocem, cuius perspicua est formatio, desidero in Wils. Lex.

Sl. 11. a. ममत्वाकृष्टचेतनः \। B ममत्वाकृष्टमानसः

Sl. 12. a. Hoc hemistichium alio modo vertere licet, ita ut शूरहस्ती *heroum-elephas* i. e. heroum optimus et सदासदः *semper-inebrius* tanquam adiectiva ad प्रधानो referas; sed loci qui nostram vertendi rationem confirmant, haud raro occurrunt.

Sl. 12. a. स। B स्वं.

Sl. 12. a. शूरहस्ती। B शूरीहस्ती.

Sl. 34. b. विषयाश्ं , यान्ति। Sic B. Ed. Calc. habet विषयश् , जातिश्. C. विषयश् , याति, चै 'वम्.

Sl. 38. a. ज्ञाने। B. ज्ञानो.

Sl. 38. a. शावचञ्चुषु। B. श्यावचञ्चुषु.

Sl. 38. b. कणमोक्षादृतान्। Perturbatum hoc atque intellectu difficillimum dictum video nunc me false separasse, nihil enim dubitandum quin कणमोक्षाद् ऋतान् sit scribendum, magis vero quid de interpretatione faciendum sit, dubitare potest; nam ablativorum istorum cumulatio efficit, ut multis rationibus queas explicare alterum hemistichium. ऋतान् ad पतगान् referri sed etiam euphonica ablativi ऋतात् mutatio esse, et ad मोहात् pertinere potest.

Sl. 39. b. एते। B. एतान्.

Sl. 40. b. संसारस्थितिकारिणा। Sic B. Ed. Calc. et C. संसारस्थितिकारिणः

Sl. 41. a. योगनिद्रा। Ab hominibus, quorum summa salus et maxima vis est in योग, in Vischnuem transferri haec animi conditio videtur, quoniam in eius cultu et religione mystica illa devotio, योग appellata, quae in Gita fuse et gravissime laudatur, exorta est. Quam sententiam seriori Indorum religionis aetati esse propriam eo colligimus tum quod notio de Vischnuis somno qui naturalem habet vim et ad tempus pluvium spectat, ad animum relatum est, tum ex योगनिद्रा ad Vischnuem translatâ ipsâ. Cum योगनिद्रा eadem ac महामाया esse dicatur, bene animadvertendum est, योगम् hic non significare summam animi perfectionem in qua mens in numine tantum defixa est, omnibus distinctis cogitationibus, omnibusque rationibus quas, sive ad res externas sive ad internas habet mens, relictis; sed notare magnam illam omniaque superantem vim, qualem is nanciscitur, qui devotionem exercet.

Sl. 41. b. एषा। C. एतत्.

Sl. 42. a. भगवती। Ed. Calc. male भवती quod etiam metrum vetat.

Sl. 43. b. मुक्तये\> Quoniam homo, dum vivit, ex Indorum opinione constrictus est naturae vinculis, itaque pura mentis essentia tum naturae impetu tum agendi studio necessario impeditur atque conturbatur, mortem quippe quae vinculorum istorum sit solutio (मुक्ति) ipsam esse et solutionem et beatitudinem facile apparebit.

Sl. 44. a. मुक्तेर्। B. मुक्तिर्.

Sl. 49. Similis sententia occurrit in H. Th. III. p. 86. ubi Wils. in adnotatione adiicit: At the intervals of the minor destructions of the world Vishnu is represented as reposing himself upon the serpent Sesha amidst the waters by which the earth is overspread. He also takes a map of four months duration from the 11th of Ashârh to the 11th of Kârtik or about the middle of June to the middle of October, or from the time the periodical rains usually commence till their termination. Cf. GHATAK. v. 3. Wils. ad Meg. p. 115.

Sl. 49. b. शेषम्। cf. Quaest. mythol.

Sl. 51. a. Hoc saepius depingitur cf. Moor H. Panth. Tab.

निद्राम् भगवतीं विष्णोर् अतुलां तेजसः प्रभुः।

Sl. 54. a. स्वाहा। Haec vox in omnibus quae Diis offeruntur sacrificiis adhibetur, quamobrem Agnis uxor स्वाहा appellatur cuius ope Dii sacrificiis fruuntur.

Sl. 54. a. स्वधा। In omnibus ad maiores sive Manes (पितृ) pertinentibus sacris summa habetur precatio. AM. MAN. III. 252. Promiscue posita videntur DEV. IV. 7. Natura, sub specie causae sive materiae omnium rerum, appellatur etiam स्वधा sive सा i. e. 8॑0¯īa quae inclusa putatur in τῷ तत् quo emphatico nomine summum numen significatur. Colebr. on the VED. p. 404, 405.

Sl. 54. a. वषट्कार। Haec vox etiam in sacrificiis cum igne adhibetur.

Sl. 54. b. त्रिधामात्रात्मिका atque

Sl. 55. a. अर्धमात्रा। Hae voces sine dubio pertinent ad artem metricam et musicam cum मात्रा syllaborum quantitatem significet. De propria et vera harum dictionum explicatiene non satis constat. Attamen levidensia quaedam apponam. Qui apud Indos numerantur septem toni (स्वर) et tres scalae musicae (ग्राम) respondent illi nostris tonis, hae diatonicis, chromaticis et enharmonicis scalis nostratium possint forsitan compa-



rari. Praeterea quae occurrunt XXI. मूर्छनानि (*tone or semitone as placed in its scale* Wils.) sine dubio aequant nostram nominandi rationem, c, cis, ces; itemque IXX. तलाः (*beating time, musical time or measure* Wils.) diversa numerorum genera v. c. <MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1779030699DEVIMAHATMYA_1-removebg-preview.png"/> ,<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1779030834DEVIMAHATMYA_2-removebg-preview.png"/>,<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1779030931DEVIMAHATMYA_3-removebg-preview.png"/>,<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1779031065DEVIMAHATMYA_4-removebg-preview.png"/> etc. Tres मात्राः quas Wils. quantitates nominat, facile non differunt a nostra <MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1779031675DEVIMAHATMYA_5-removebg-preview.png"/>divisione. Neque minus tria स्थानानि similia sunt nostris intervallis magnis (grofse) parvis (*kleine*) et extensis (*übermäfsig*). Qui numerantur tres लयाः (*equal time in music* Wils.) sine dubio ad rhythmos spectant, neque minus haesitandum est in यतयः quas Wils. pausas explicat. Novem रसाः (*taste,* *sentiment*, *emotion*, *as an object of* *composition* Wils.) comparandi sunt cum nostris Largo, Adagio, Andante, Maestoso etc. Praeterea afferuntur XXXVI. वर्णाः (*musical mode* Wils.) XL. भाषा *one of the* रागिणी (*modification of a musical mode of which five are assigned to each mode* Wils.) et CL. गीता (*sung*) Wils.

Sl. 55. b. सा त्वम्। B. सन्ध्या.

Sl. 55. b. सा et सावित्री। Cf. quae in nostris Quaestionibus mythologicis de Sûryo diximus.

Sl. 55. b. देवि जननी। B. वेदजननी.

Sl. 56. a. विश्वम्। C. सर्वे.

Sl. 56. a. b. Ex eiusmodi aliisque in Cant. IV. et XI. prolatis sententiis sicut ex universi carminis tenore colligendum est, doctrinam de Devia in hoc carmine professam, sectae esse propriam, cum Devia non solum in se naturam et potentiam omnium Deorum Dearumque contineat, sed etiam (v. 65.) ipsius trinitatis causa et origo laudatur.

**CANTUS II.**

Sl. 1. a. देवासुरम्। De Asurorum et Deorum bello in epicis carminibus multifariam fit mentio cf. RAM. SER. III. 76. 4. Unde Asuri et Suri sive Dii nomen acceperint patet e RAM. SCHL. I. 45. ubi de Ambrosiae origine multisque aliis ex agitatione oceani exortis rebus disseritur et deinde adiicetur v. 36, 37, 38.

वरुणस्य ततः कन्या वारुणी रघुनन्दन।  
उत्पपात रसात् तस्मान् मार्गमाणा प्रतिग्रहम्॥३६॥

दितेः पुत्रा न तां राम जगृहुर् वरुणात्मजाम्।  
अदितेस् तु सुता वीर जगृहुस् ताम् अनिन्दिताम्॥३७॥

सुराप्रतिग्रहाद् देवाः सुरा इत्य् अभिविश्रुताः।  
अप्रतिग्रहणात् तस्या दैतेयाश् चा'सुरास् तथा॥३८॥

„Varuni deinde filia Vârunia, o Raghuis-proles, exsurrexit e fluido illo, quaerens „electionem; Ditiae filii, non hanc, o Rame, elegerunt Varuni-filiam, Aditiae „autem nati, o heros, elegerunt illam praeclaram; potus-(Surâ) electione Dii „Suri ita celebrati *sunt*, non-electione illius Ditiae-nati etiam Asuri *nominati* „*sunt.*"

Sl. 1. b. Hoc hemistichium metrum excedit una syllaba, medela in promptu est si च eiicimus sed, omnibus Cod. consentientibus, conservare maluimus.

**CANTUS V.**

Sl. 1. *b.* मदबलाश्रयात्। Observanda est haec structura, occurrit etiam RAM. SER. I. 47. 22. ubi haec sunt verba तपोब्रह्मबलाश्रयात् C. habet मदनबलाश्रयात्.

Sl. 3. *a.* ताव् एव। B. तथैव.

Sl. 3. *a.* पवनर्धिं \। De पवन cf. Quaest. mythol. de अनिल.

Sl. 5. *a.* यथा। Observanda est huius vocis usus, cum Graecorum *õτι* instar ad inducendum sermonem positum sit.

Sl. 6. *a.* हिमवन्तम्। हिमवत् *nive-praeditus.* Hoc est nomen illius montis qui divino honore colitur. Duas filias quas Mena montis Meruis filia procreavit, ipsi tribuunt, Umam et Gangam, quarum hanc, Diis rogantibus, Rudro (Sivo) dedit uxorem. RAM. SCHL. I. 36. 14. ibid. v. 13. appellatur धातुनाम् आकरो महान् *metallorum fodina magna.* Vocabula ॥ देवा ऊचुः ॥ versui septimo praeponenda C. non habet.

Sl. 9. *b.* नैर्ऋत्यै भूभृताम्। Genius est regionis meridie occasum versus *(südwestlich)* MAN. XI. 104, 119.

 Cum notiones de Diis, qui singulis regionibus praesunt, incertae sint, annotationem quam de hac re illustr. Wilsonius adiicit in H. Th. II. p. 39. apponimus.

 The Lokapâlas or Guardians of the world are sometimes confounded with the Deities presiding over the different cardinal points, but this is not quite correct, and they are more properly the divinities who were appointed by Brahmâ upon the creation of the world, to act as rulers over the different kinds of created things: the list occurs in several Puranas, but the following is from the Mahâbhârat, the Harivansa portion.

 Indra. Sovereign of the three Lokas, or Earth and the Regions above and below.

 Soma—of sacrifices, ascetic rites, the lunar and solar asterisms, Brahmans and healing herbs.

 Daksha—of the Prajâpatis the patriarchs or first created and progenitors of mankind.

 Varuna—of the Waters.

 Vaisvânara—of the Pîtris or Manes.

 Vâyu—of the Gandherbas, of unembodied element, of time and sound.

 Mahâdeva—of the Mâtris, of the spirits of ill, of kine, of portents and planets, of infirmities and diseases, and of Ghosts.

 Vaisravana—of the Yakshas, Rakshasas, Guhyakas, of wealth and of all precious gems.

 Sesha—of the entire Serpent race.

 Vasuki—of the Nagas or Ophite tribes of Pâtâla.

 Takshaka—younger brother of the Adityas, of Snakes.

 Parjânya—of Oceans, rivers, clouds, and rain.

 Chitraratha—of the Ganderbhas.

 Kâmadeva—of the Apsarases.

 Nandi the bull of Siva, of all quadrupeds.

 Hiranyâksha and Hiranyâkasipu, of the Daityas.

 Viprachitti—of the Dânavas.

 Mahâkâla—of the Ganas or Siva's attendants.

 Vritra—of the children of Anâyusha the wife of Twashtri.

 Râhu the son Sìnhikâ—of evil portents and prodigies.

 Samvatsara—of the divisions of time from the twinkling of an eye to the period of an age.

 Superna—of Birds of prey.

 Garura—of the winged race.

 Aruna—the brother of Garura was made by Indra, ruler in the East.

 Yama the son of Aditya in the South.

 The son of Kasyapa, Amburaja, in the West.

 Pingala the son of Pulastya in the North.

 Having thus nominated the Presiding Spirits, various Lokas or districts were created by Swayambhu—as brilliant as the sun or fire, radiant as lightning, or chastely beaming as the Moon, of various colours, moveable at will, many hundreds of Yojanas in extent, the fit abodes of the pious, exempt from sin and pain. Those Brahmans whose merit shines conspicuous are elevated to these regions, those who practice piety and worship devoutly, who are upright and benevolent, free from cupidity and cherishers of the poor.

 Having thus distributed his sons, Brahma departed to his own dwelling Pushkara. The Deities rambled through the districts, and engaged in the charges respectively assigned them, being all cherished by Mahendra. The Gods, with Indra at their head, as placed by Swayambhu discharging their guardian duties obtained fame and heaven, and receiving their share of sacrifices enjoyed prosperity and happiness.

 Some of the early sections of the Kâsi k'hand of the Skânda Purana or from the 9th to the 23d contain a description of the several Lokas, the cities or spheres of the different divinities as they are traversed by Sivasermâ on his way from earth to the region of Siva.

 He passes in this route the Lokas of the nymphs, of the Sun, of Indra, Agni, Nirrhita, Varuna, Vâyu, Kuvera, of the Ganas or attendants of Siva, of Soma, of the lunar asterisms, of Budha Sukra, Bhauma, Guru and Sani or the planets Mercury, Venus, Mars, Jupiter and Saturn, of the seven Rishis, of Dhruva, the Lokas called Maharloka, Janaloka and Tapoloka, and that called Satyaloka, the abode of Brahma, and Vaikuntha and Kailas or the regions severally of Vishnu and Siva. This disposition of the spheres howewer has evidently received a peculiar colouring from the Pauranic Cosmography, and the sectarial bias of the Skânda Purâna.

Sl. 10. *a.* सर्वकारिण्यै \। B. सर्वकारिणि.

Sl. 35. *b.* व्याप्त्यै। C. व्याप्ति. B. व्याप्तै.

Sl. 39. *b.*जाह्नवी। Gangae fluminis cognomen. Originem in terra ex desiderio Bhagirathi ducit, qui maiores suos Sagaridos sanctae illius aquae libatione liberare eisque coelum parare studuit, devotioneque contigit, ut Gangam de coelo in terram deduceret. Quae eum secuta inundabat locum sacrificii Dschanuis qui iratus illam absorpsit et Deorum solis precibus commotus, per aures dimisit, inde cognomina Gangae भागीरथी atque जाह्नवी RAM. SCHL. I. 44. 48. In tartaro (पाताल) nominatur भोगवती RAM. SCHL. I. 5. 20. et quia in coelo, in terra, et in inferis fluere putatur: त्रिपथगा नदी *tribus-viis-incedens flumen* RAM. SCHL. I. 36. 16. सरितां श्रेष्ठा मुनिसेविता पुण्यसलिला हन्ससारससेविता *fluminum optimum, a sapientibus habitatum, purâ-aquâ, anseribus-et gruibus-tectum* ibid. v. 7. समुद्रमहिषी *maris-uxor* DILUV. 18. Cum Gangae aqua omnia auferat peccata, appellatur लोकपावनी *mundi-lustramen* ibid. v. 17.

Sl. 62. *b.* गजरत्नं च हृतम्। C. जगरत्नानि हृत्व.

Sl. 63. *a.* क्षीरोदमथनोद्भूतम्। Haud alienum videtur nobis, hic fabulam de agitatione oceani ex Gitae editione illustr. Wilkins describere. Rameis eandem offert (RAM. SCHL. I. 45.) sed ea in re praecipue differt, ut vim salutarem quam Vischnus in Mahâbhârato habet, in Sivum transferat.

 Episode from the Mahâbhârata Book I. Chap. 15.

 There is a fair and stately mountain, and its name it Mêru, a most exalted mass of glory, reflecting the sunny rays from the splendid surface of its gilded horns. It is cloathed in gold, and is the respected haunt of Dêws and Gandharvs. It is inconceivable, and not to be encompassed by sinful man; and it is guarded by dreadful serpents. Many celestial medicinal plants adorn its sides, and it stands, piercing the heavens with its aspiring summit, a mighty hill inaccessible even by the human mind! It is adorned with trees and pleasant streams, and resoundeth with the delightful songs of various birds. The Soors and all the glorious hosts of heaven, having ascended to the summit of this lofty mountain, sparkling with precious gems, and for eternal ages raised, were sitting in solemn synod, meditating the discovery of the Amreeta, or water of immortality. The Dêw Nârâyan being also there, spoke unto Brahmâ, whilst the Soors were thus consulting together, and said, ,,Let the ocean, as a pot of milk, be churned by the united ,,labour of the Soors and Asoors; and when the mighty waters have been stirred ,,up, the Amreeta shall be found. Let them collect together every medicinal herb ,,and every precious thing, and let them stir the ocean, and they shall discover the ,,Amreeta.'' There is also another mighty mountain whose name is Mandar, ant its rocky summits are like towering clouds. It is cloathed in a net of the entangled tendrils of the twining creeper, and resoundeth with the harmony of various birds. Innumerable savage beasts infest its borders, and it is the respected haunt of Keennars, Dews, and Apsars. It standeth eleven thousand Yojan above the earth, and eleven thousand more below its surface.

 As the united bands of Dêws were unable to remove this mountain, they went before Veeshnoo who was sitting with Brahmâ, and addressed them in these words: ,,Exert, O masters, your most superior wisdom to remove the mountain Mandar, ,,and employ your utmost power for our good.''

 Veeshnoo and Brahmâ having said, ,,It shall be according to your wish'', he with the lotus eye directed the king of Serpents to appear; and Ananta arose, and was instructed in that work by Brahmâ, and commanded by Nârâyan to perform it. Then Ananta, by his power, took up that king of mountains, together with all its forests and every inhabitant thereof; and the Soors accompanied him into the presence of the Ocean, whom they addressed, saying, ,,We will stir up thy waters to ,,obtain the Amreeta.'' And the Lord of the waters replied— ,,Let me also have ,,a share, seeing I am to bear the violent agitations that will be caused by the whir- ,,ling of the mountain.'' Then the Soors and the Asoors spoke unto Koormaraja, the king of the Tortoises, upon the strand of the ocean, and said — ,,My Lord is able ,,to be the supporter of this mountain.'' The Tortoise replied, ,,Be it so:'' and it was placed upon his back.

 So the mountain being set upon the back of the Tortoise, Eendra began to whirl it about as it were a machine. The mountain Mandar served as a churn, and the serpent Vasookee for the rope; and thus in former days did the Dêws, the Asoors, and the Dânoos, begin to stir up the waters of the ocean for the discovery of the Amreeta. The mighty Asoors were employed on the side of the serpent's head, whilst all the Soors assembled about his tail. Ananta, that sovereign Dêw, stood near Nârâyan. They now pull forth the serpent's head repeatedly, and as often let it go; whilst there issued from his mouth, thus violently drawing to and from by the Soors and Asoors, a continual stream of fire, and smoke, and wind; which ascending in thick clouds replete with lightning, it began to rain down upon the heavenly bands, who were already fatigued with their labour; whilst a shower of flowers was shaken from the top of the mountain, covering the heads of all, both Soors and Asoors. In the mean time the roaring of the ocean, whilst violently agitated with the whirling of the mountain Mandar by the Soors and Asoors, was like the bellowing of a mighty cloud. —Thousands of the various productions of the waters were torn to pieces by the mountain, and confounded with the briny flood; and every specific being of the deep, and all the inhabitants of the great abyss which is below the earth, were annihilated; whilst, from the violent agitation of the mountain, the forest trees were dashed against each other, and precipitated from its utmost height, with all the birds thereon; from whose violent confrication a raging fire was produced, involving the whole mountain with smoke and flame, as with a dark blue cloud, and the lightning's vivid flash. The lion and the retreating elephant are overtaken by the devouring flames, and every vital being, and every specific thing, are consumed in the general conflagration.

 The raging flames, thus spreeding destruction on all sides, were at length quenched by a shower of cloud-borne water poured down by the immortal Eendra. And now a heterogeneous stream of the concocted juices of various trees and plants ran down into the briny flood. It was from this milk-like stream of juices produced from those trees and plants, and a mixture of melted gold, that the Soors obtained their immortality.

 The waters of the ocean now being assimilated with those juices, were converted into milk, and from that milk a kind of butter was presently produced; when the heavenly bands went again into the presence of Brahmâ, the granter of boons, and addressed him, saying— ,,Except Nârâyan, every other Soor and Asoor is ,,fatigued with his labour, and still the Amreeta doth not appear; wherefore the ,,churning of the ocean is at a stand.'' Then Brahmâ said unto Nârâyan. ,,Endue ,,them with recruited strength, for thou art their support.'' And Nârâyan answered and said— ,,I will give fresh vigour to such as co-operate in the work. Let ,,Mandar be whirled about, and the bed of the ocean be kept steady.'' When they heard the words of Nârâyan they all returned again to the work, and began to stir about with great force that butter of the ocean; when there presently arose from out the troubled deep—first the moon, with a pleasing countenance, shining with ten thousand beams of gentle light; next fellowed Sree, the Goddess of fortune, whose seat is the white bily of the waters; then Soorâ-Dêvee, the Goddess of wine, and the wite horse called Oochisrava. And after these there was produced, from the unctuous mass, the jewel Kowstoobh, that glorious sparkling gem worn by Nârâyan on his breast; so Pâreejât, the tree of plenty, and Soorabhee, the cow that granted every heart's desire.

 The moon, Soorâ-Dêwee, the Goddess Sree, and the horse as swift as thought, instantly marched away towards the Dêws, keeping in the path of the sun.

 Then the Dêw Dhanwantaree, in human shape, came forth, holding in his hand a white vessel filled with the immortal juice Amreeta. When the Asoors beheld these wondrous things appear, they raised their tumultuous voices for the Amreeta, and each of them clamorously exclaimed— ,,This of right is mine!''

 In the mean time Irâvat, a mighty elephant, arose, now kept by the God of thunder; and as they continued to churn the ocean more than enough, that deadly poison issued from its bed, burning like a raging fire, whose dreadful fumes in a moment spread throughout the world, confounding the three regions of the universe with its mortal stench; until Seeva at the word of Brahmâ, swallowed the fatal drug to save mankind; which remaining in the throat of that sovereign Dêw of magic form, from that time he hath been called Neel-Kant, because his throat was stained blue.

 When the Asoors beheld this miraculous deed, they became desperate, and the Amreeta and the Goddess Sree became the source of endless hatred.

 Then Nârâyan assumed the character and person of Môheenee Mâyâ, the power of inchantment, in a female form of wonderful beauty, and stood before the Asoors; whose minds being fascinated by her presence, and deprived of reason, they seized the Amreeta, and gave it unto her. The Asoors now cloath themselves in costly armour, and, seizing their various weapons, rush on together to attack the Soors. In the mean time Nârâyan, in the female form, having obtained the Amreeta from the hands of their leader, the hosts of Soors, during the tumult and confusion of the Asoors, drank of the living water. And it so fell out, that whilst the Soors were quenching their thirst for immortality, Râhoo, an Asoor, assumed the form of a Soor, and began to drink also. And the water had but reached his throat, when the sun and moon, in friendship to the Soors, discovered the deceit; and instantly Nârâyan cut off his head, as he was drinking, with his splendid weapon Chakra. And the gigantic head of the Asoor, emblem of a mountain's summit, being thus separated from his body by the Chakras edge, bounded into the heavens with a dreadful cry, whilst his ponderous trunk fell cleaving the ground asunder, and shaking the whole earth unto its foundation, with all its islands, rocks, and forests. And from that time the head of Râhoo resolved an eternal enmity, and continueth, even unto this day, at times to seize upon the sun and moon.

 Now Nârâyan, having quitted the female figure he had assumed, began to disturb the Asoors with sundry celestial weapons; and from that instant a dreadful battle was commenced, on the ocean's briny strand, betwen the Asoors and the Soors. Innumerable sharp and missile weapons were hurled, and thousands of piercing darts and battle-axes fell on all sides. The Asoors vomit blood from the wounds of the Chakra, and fall upon the ground pierced by the sword, the spear, and spiked club. —Heads, glittering with polished gold, divided by the Pattee's blade, drop incessantly; and mangled bodies, wallowing in their gore, lay like fragments of mighty rocks sparkling with gems and precious ores. Millions of sighs and groans arise on every side; and the sun is overcast with blood, as they clash their arms, and wound each other with their dreadful instruments of destruction.

 Now the battle's fought with the iron-spiked club, and, as they close, with clenched fist; and the din of war ascendeth to the heavens! They cry— ,,Pursue! ,,strike! fell to the ground!'' so that a horrid and tumultuous noise is heard on all sides.

 In the midst of this dreadful hurry and confusion of the fight, Nar and Nârâyan entered the field together. Nârâyan beholding a celestial bow in the hand of Nar, it reminded him of his Chakra, the destroyer of the Asoors. The faithful weapon, by name Soodarsan, ready at the mind's call, flew down from heaven with direct and refulgent speed, beautiful, yet terrible to behold. And being arrived, glowing like the sacrificial flame, and spreading terror around, Nârâyan, with his right arm formed like the elephantine trunk, hurled forth the ponderous orb, the speedy messenger, and glorious ruin of hostile towns; who, raging like the final all-destroying fire, shot bounding with desolating force, killing thousand of the Asoors in his rapid flight, burning and involving, like the lambent flame, and cutting down all that would oppose him. Anon he climbeth the heavens, and now again darteth into the field like a Peesâch to feast in blood.

 Now the dauntless Asoors strive, with repeated strength, to crush the Soors with rocks and mountains, which, hurled in vast numbers into the heavens, appeared like scattered clouds, and fell, with all the trees thereon, in millions of fear- exciting torrents, striking violently against each other with a mighty noise; and in their fall the earth, with all its fields and forests, is driven from its foundation: they thunder furiously at each other as they roll along the field, and spend their strength in mutual conflict.

 Now Nar, seeing the Soors overwhelmed with fear, filled up the path to heaven with showers of golden-headed arrows, and split the mountain summits with his unerring shafts; and the Asoors, finding themselves again sore pressed by the Soors, precipetately flee: some rush headlong into the briny waters of the ocean, and others hide themselves within the bowels of the earth.

 The rage of the glorious Chakra, Soodarsan, which for a while burnt like the oil-fed fire, now grew cool, and he retired into the heavens from whence he came. And the Soors having obtained the victory, the mountain Mandar was carried back to its former station with great respect; whilst the waters also retired, filling the firmament and the heavens with their dreadful roarings. The Soors guarded the Amreeta with great care, and rejoiced exceedingly because of their success; and Eendra, with all his immortal bands, gave the water of life unto Nârâyan, to keep it for their use.''

**CANTUS VIII.**

Sl. 12. *a.* De गुह cf. Quaest. mythol.

Sl. 12. *a.* शक्तयः \। Haec notio, ex qua mens discernit inter argumentum et formam, inter Deum eiusque significationem sola ei aetati est propria, qua mens philosophicis intenta quaestionibus, illa simplice fide relicta, sciens cogitatione id persequitur in quod antea sua sponte incubuit. Indorum ingenium lubenter eiusmodi quaestionibus indulget, fideique et cultus formis cogitationes involvit et quodcunque fingendi creavit vi, id meditandi vi dissolvit. Utramque rationem Indi summo studio persecuti sunt.

 Illustr. Colebrookius haec affert As. Res. VIII. p. 82.

 The eight Sactis or energie of as many Deities, are also called Mátris or mothers. They are named Bráhmi, etc. because the issued from the bodies of Bráhma and the other gods respectively (Raya Mucuta on theAmeracosha). In some places, they are thus enumerated: Bráhmí, Máhéśwarí, Aindrí, Váráhí, Vaishnáví, Caumárí, Chámun'dá and Charchicá. However, some authorities reduce the number to seven; omiting Chámunn'dá and Charchicá; but inserting Cauvérí.

 Prayers are addressed to the Mátris on various occasions; especially in the Cavachas, or defensive incantations. I shall cite two by way of example; and subjoin extracts from the Márcan ́deya purán ́a, descriptive of these goddesses.

 ,,May Brahmání, conferring the benefit of all benedictions, protect me on the east; and Náráyan'í, on the south-east, for the sake of realising every wish Máhéśwarí too, on the south, rendering every thing auspicious; Chámun'da, on the south- east, discomfiting all enemies; and, on the west, Caumárí, armed with her lance and slayer of foes: on the north-west, Aparájitá, the beauteous giver of Victory; on the north, Váráhí, granter of boons: and on the north-east, Nárasinhí, the banisher of terrour. May these mothers, being eight Deities and active powers, defend me.''

 Another incantation simply enumerates the same eight goddesses, and proceeds thus: may these and all Mátris guard me with their respective weapons, on all quarters and on every point.

 Deinde sequitur versio octo versuum 14-22. nostrae editionis.

Sl. 38. *a.* Post प्राप्ते B. habet हि.

Sl. 39. *a.* De नन्द et यशोदा cf. BRAHMA-VAIV. Praef. p. 6, 7.

Sl. 41. *b.* रक्ता \। B. रक्त.

Sl. 45. *a.* भरिष्यामि। B. भविष्यामि.

Sl. 46. *a.* दुर्गम् आख्यम्। Coniunge haec verba, cum आख्य solum in compositis usurpetur.

Sl. 47. *b.* भक्षयिष्यामि। C. क्षययिष्यामि.

Sl. 49. *b.* कृत्वा सङ्ख्येय षट्पदम्। Lege कृत्वा सङ्ख्येयषट्पदम् sive 'सङ्ख्येयषट्पदम् conf. NAL. XXI. 9.

**————**

**CANTUS XII.**

Sl. 4. *b.* दारिद्रयम्। C. दारिद्रं.

Sl. 5. *a.* तस्य। B. तेषाम्.

Sl. 5. *b.* शस्त्र \। B. शास्त्र.

Sl. 6. *b.* हि तत्। B. महत्.

Sl. 13. *a.* उत्पत्रीश् च तथा \। C. et Ed. Calc. तथा चोत्पत्रयः

Sl. 23. *b.* तास् \। B. यास्.

Sl. 28. *b.* पलायन्ते। B. पलयन्ते.

Sl. 29. *b.* अन्तरधीयत। B. अन्तरधीयते.

Sl. 31. *b.* पातालम्। पाताल est Tartarus, in quo quatuor mundum gestantes elephanti stant: in oriente विरुपाक्ष cuius capitis motu, terrae motus exoritur; in meridie महापद्म, in occidente सौमनस, in septentrione भद्र sive हिमपाण्डुर. RAM. SCHL. I. 41. 14-22. Praeterea viginti et unus enumerantur Orci. MAN. IV. 88, 89, 90.

Sl. 33. *b.* तुष्टा ऋद्धिम्। De neglecta euphoniae regula cf. Colebr. Gram. pag. 21.

Sl. 34. *b.* महाकाल्या महाकाले। B. महालक्ष्म्या महाकाल्या. महाकाले significatur illa aetas qua mundus consumitur.

Sl. 34. *a.* et *b.* काले। Eodem modo usurpatur RAM. SER. III. 76. 97. B. habet काली.

**————**

**CANTUS XIII.**

Sl. 1. *a.* राजन्। C. et B. भूप.

Sl. 2. *b.* तया। C. त्वया.

Sl. 8. *b.* उक्षितम्। Ed. Calc. उच्छितम्.

Sl. 13. *a.* स्वं राज्यम्। C. स्वराज्यम्.

**————**
